  11. I'm writing this review because I was on the fence about whether or not to buy this product and wanted to provide some helpful info for others considering it. Overall, I'm very happy with the product and I get good results. FIRST, let me say that the first time you use this, IT WILL HURT. Before the first use, I let the hair on my legs grow out quite a bit and then trimmed with the included shaver head to the suggested length for optimal epilation (in the instruction manual). Then I started with the epilator head and I about cried in pain and wondered why in the bleep did I buy this thing?!? I was determined to finish, though, so I endured the pain. I did get red spots on my legs where the hair was pulled, but the spots were completely gone by the next day and they only seem to appear now when the hair is longer or denser (i.e. going longer between epliating sessions). The epilator does not remove EVERY SINGLE HAIR, so if your objective is baby butt smooth legs, this product may not be for you. However, the hairs it leaves are very fine and very short and not noticeable to the eye, but only to touch. This is acceptable to me. The included shaver attachment works very well, so you could run the shaver over your legs after epilating if you need a very smooth finish.<br /><br />I read in other reviews that after epilating, the hair grows back slower and finer. I did not believe this, because with shaving it seems the opposite is true. I can attest that with epilating, the hair does, indeed, grow back slower and finer. I am very pleased with this aspect of epilation.<br /><br />I have experienced some ingrown hairs that present like tiny pimples. To help prevent this, I use exfoliating bath/shower gloves everyday on my legs to remove any excess dead/dry skin. These gloves are available at a very reasonable price on amazon.<br /><br />Finally, pain greatly diminishes on subsequent uses because there are fewer hairs each time you epilate. I don't mind thepain at all now that I've been using it for a few months.<br /><br />I have not used it on my underarms or bikini area, so I cannot comment on its effectiveness in those areas.<br /><br />OVERALL, I'm very happy with this product and consider it money well spent.

  16. A review on the Philips HP6576/50 Satin Perfect Deluxe Epilator, and not a story about my first epilating experience:<br /><br />The first thing I noticed about the epilator before even taking it out of the box was the beautiful design. Instead of a boring solid color print(s), the epilator sports a gorgeous white base color with a floral print on the front - very classy. The see-through \\"glass\\" (it is actually plastic) effect on the front is also very attracting. The cosmetic aspect of the epilator is definitely a plus in my book.<br /><br />Onto the actual product, the epilator is nice middle ground weight. From this, you can get a good grip and can control precise motions. The feel of the epilator is okay, but I think Philips could have done better. I believe the outside of the body is made entirely of plastic, which makes it feel cheaper than you would guess. I also would have liked it better if there was a grip piece on both sides. The epilator hasn't slipped from my hands yet during epilating, but an actual grip would provide better security. On the front, you can find the OptiLight and the \\"on\\" button. Honestly, my first impression of the OptiLight was terrible. I thought that it would be great for someone who would use the epilator in the dark (for some strange reason...) However, after using the epilator for a while, I absolutely love it. The OptiLight allows you to see even the tiniest and lightest hairs(which is great for me because I have dark hair.) Even in a well-lit room, the OptiLight never fails to impress me. The light is very bright and has good spread [distance.] Moving to the \\"on\\" button, I have only one thing to say about it. Okay -- maybe more because of my explanation. I really, absolutely dislike the button. It looks nice and fits in with the cosmetic theme, but the button does not meet my Philip expectations. It is a single push button, so you basically click the button for every function - turning it on/off and switching the power settings. First of all, using just one button for everything will wear down the epilator more easily. The epilator may not have as much life as one that has a \\"switch\\" type of button (where you go up or down depending on the preferred speed.) If I wanted just to epilate my underarms, I would have to click twice just to get to the lower speed setting. For someone that may have sensitive skin to begin with and needs the lower setting every single time, this would be a hassle. The push button I think is an incredibly stupid design. Another downfall of the push button is the \\"effectiveness\\" of switching to the lower setting. When first turning on the epilator and going straight to the second speed setting, or switching over to the lower speed setting while the epilator is on, it is sometimes difficult to know whether you have successfully selected the setting (the sound difference between the two speeds is very minimal so this may be hard to determine success.) This means that I will always have to pick up my epilator (if I am already epilating this is a pain) and look at the front to see if I am in the right speed setting. My dislike for the button does not really affect the epilator performance, but I think that feature could have been better thought out.<br /><br />Though the epilator itself works very well, the bonus attachments that come with the deluxe model provide a more optimal performance. There are a total of 4 attachments, each of which comes very handy. I absolutely love the active hair lifter attachment, especially on my legs - as the hairs tend to lay flat. I also find that there is more hair pickup than without the attachment, so I don't have to run my epilator over the same area as much. The active massaging system with pivoting cap attachment also works really well. This is my favorite attachment out of the whole set because the pain from epilating is slightly diminished. However, I wish that the massagers were also \\"active\\" as well, like the massager on the active hair lifter attachment. I feel that if the massagers were self-rotating, this would provide even more comfort when epilating. Aside from that, I really love the attachment. It also speeds up my epilating time because I feel less pain and can tolerate my epilator running over my skin for a longer period. Last but not least, there is the shaving/trimming attachment. I think these attachments boost the value of the epilator. If for some reason I had a skin irritation, and did not want to risk the effect of plucking my hairs out in that spot, I could use the shaving attachment. For hair that may be too long for optimum epilating, the trimming attachment could be used. Generally speaking, the shaving attachment is convenient for someone who prefers shaving a certain area over epilating, and the trimming attachment is great to trim down any long hairs. Overall, each attachment offers an improved epilating experience. They speed up the process, decrease pain, and may even replace your shaver.<br /><br />Another bonus that comes with the deluxe model is the Illuminating Smart Tweezers. I do not care much for this; the concept is good, but I find my cheap 99 cent tweezers from Dillions does a better job. There is an \\"OptiLight\\" - which initially seems great because it never seems we can get good lighting to pluck and maintain our eyebrows. However, the light - which is located in between the two clamps of the tweezers - is very bright. No matter how many times I try to motivate myself to use the tweezers, I cannot find a way to utilize them so that I am not blinded by the light. For people that can use the tweezers however, the light pinpoints a specific area extremely well. Because of the placement of the OptiLight, a tight grip is required to clamp down on individual hairs. I also feel that the tweezers' shape or cut does not work as well as my other tweezers. The mirror that is included is a great tool to go along with the tweezers. It has great zoom - probably a2 or even 3x zoom. This is great because it is no longer a hassle to go very close to a bathroom mirror for those stubborn hairs. The packaging of the tweezers is okay, but not terrific. There is risk of scratching the mirror as you place the tweezers back into the container. Also, I feel like I will damage either the mirror or the tweezers every time I open or close the container. It would have been smart to integrate a twist feature (like that of a water bottle) or a snap lock.<br /><br />I feel that some people would not care about this, but I think it something worth mentioning. The charger seems really cheap; it is really light (which could be a good thing for some) and made out of plastic. I wish the appearance - material and shape - had been better. Also, I was initially very afraid that I received a dud. However, the charger should work, but you must first hear a big CLICK sound when you plug the cord into your epilator. I made the mistake of being too gentle and didn't push it in hard enough. Then (I really love this part), a pretty battery shaped light will be lit on the front of the epilator. It will pulse for certain duration and the light will disappear for the rest of the time, until after the epilator is completely charged. It does not take long at all for the epilator to charge. I believe it only takes around an hour.<br /><br />One thing that may not bother a lot of people but bothers me is the travel case/pouch that comes in the box. It's great for stuffing all of my equipment in there - my epilator, tweezers, attachments, and charger. And exactly like what it would sound like, you will run the risk of damaging something. The thing I am most worried about is the actual epilator. The pouch is very very thin and is not padded, so it is basically a bag where you throw in your items. Not to mention it barely fits all of the items. I will most likely use the pouch for the attachments and the charger, and will probably use a separate makeup bag to storemy epilator. At the minimal the pouch could have had separate pockets.<br /><br />Overall: I cannot speak for all epilators (this is my first), but I can gather from my personal experience [with the Philips Satin Perfect Deluxe Epilator (HP6576/50)] that this is a great epilator. Spending a bit more money with the deluxe model will grant you a few bonuses, but the product works really well by itself (Philips HP6576/60 Satin Perfect Epilator). The Philips Satin Perfect Epilator is a bit overpriced, but it can be a good investment to make. It will meet all your expectations if you can look past the little details. I definitely recommend this to anyone who is looking for a reliable epilator. It can also be used cordlessly -- definitely a plus. I would also recommend the deluxe model, as you are getting a multifunctional tool (epilator and shaver) that you will absolutely love. This baby will not be going anywhere, and I hope it lasts a really long time.<br /><br />Sincerely,<br />An unbiased BzzAgent -- going into epilating without any prior experience and not reading the specialties before hand<br /><br />** I DO RECOMMEND THAT ALL INSRUCTIONS SHOULD BE READ BEFORE DOING ANYTHING, IN ORDER TO CORRECTLY USE AND CARE FOR YOUR EPILATOR!**

I have never used an epilator before, to tell you the truth when I was chosen to try this I had to actually look up what an epilator was! After reading about it I have to admit I was a little scared and my first thought was Ouch! For those of you who don't know, an epilator, in basic terms is an electrical device (looks like an electric shaver) used to remove hair by grasping multiple hairs simultaneously (think a bunch of tiny little tweezers) and pulling them out by the root. Now the fun part (Well um maybe)..... After I let my epilator fully charge I was ready to give this bad boy a try. I prepped my legs by exfoliating because I thought it might help to soften the hair follicle and help with any ingrown hairs I may have. I fully dried my legs since the directions state not to use on wet hair. I chose to use the Optimal Performance Cap since this was my first time ever using an epilator. Okay I was now prepped and ready. I turned the device on before using it just to see how it worked. I was not expecting it to be as loud as it was! This scared me a little more seeing how fast those little tweezers were moving. There are two speeds. The faster one is for larger areas such as your legs and the slower one is for smaller areas such as your underarms. Simply press the on/off button once to turn on the device (this is the high speed); press again (this is the slow speed); press one more time and it turns the device off. You want to start epilating by placing the epilator on your leg at a 90 degree angle with the on/off button pointing in the direction your are going to move the device. Hold the skin taught as you slowly move the device up your leg.........Okay here I go....OUCH! This is painful and you can actually feel the hair being pulled out by the root! First pass I was squinting my eyes in pain thinking \\"really why torture yourself like this\\"? Second pass, okay this seems to be getting a little more tolerable with the occasional pulls hurting more than others. About 2 minutes into it I have to say I did get use to the pain (a little). I found that it took me about 15-20 minutes to do one leg. After inspection the epilator did miss many hairs. I actually went back through with the lighted tweezers and started to pluck the missed hairs. Eeekkk my legs were super red and I was scared that it was not gonna go away! So I decided to wait a bit before proceeding onto my other leg. After about 45 minutes the rednessdid start to fade a lot so I finished the second leg. Fast forward to a week later.... Wow! I am in total shock that my legs are still smooth (besides the little hairs the epilator missed and the hairs I missed plucking)! I normally use a reusable manual razor and have to shave every 2 days! This alone makes me want to continue to use the epilator as my new means to shaving. Even though I have yet to use the epilator on my underarms (I'm a scaredy cat) I am building up the courage to do so so I do not have to shave them every 2 days as well! As far as the bikini area...forget that, that is totally out of the question for me! Regular shaving in that area for me! So in summary... After a little bit of pain I would definitely recommend that you give the Philips Satin Perfect Epilator a try (only if you have some tolerance for pain). I am planning on updating my blog when the hair on my legs does start to grow back since I have heard that epilation can cause ingrown hairs. A few I can deal with but if epilation gives me many ingrown hairs I may have to discontinue use even though I absolutely love not having to shave every 2 days! I will also give you an update when I use the epilator on my underarms (eeek)!

While it did work at removing hair, it got sticky. Then as it warmed in my hand, it stuck to my leg and gave me a HUGE bruise when I tried pull it off. I tried products like Nair....didn't even dissolve one hair, and it irritated my sensitive skin. By this point I was so frustrated, I started looking up laser hair removal. Come to find out, I am not a candidate for it because my leg hairs are red and blonde. Could my luck get any worse?! Then I found these things called epilators. They sounded like machines created by the devil himself, but I was willing to try it. After much research and youtube videos, this seemed like the best one. I ordered it. And as soon as it arrived, I tore into the box and charged it. I have read and heard that it can hurt like heck. But I have put my body through a lot already with tattoos, body piercings including my tongue, and child birth with no epidural, so I thought I could handle it. I put a washcloth in my mouth to bite down on just in case though :)<br />I started on the bottom of my right leg, and yes, it did hurt some. It felt like when I was getting my tattoo or someone repeatedly flicking me with a rubberband but tolerable. My leg hairs were only able 1-1.5mm long. But when they were being pulled out, they were about 1/4in long, so I could tell that they were really being pulled out from the root instead of being broken off. I'm not saying that no hairs were broken off, some may have, but I saw a lot lf hairs that were pulled out. I started out using the efficiency head, but then moved to the head that lifts up the hairs. I actually think this one works best at cutting down the pain.<br />This is a great machine, and I am greatful I found it. I love the different attachments, and the tweezers. The light on the epilator is a life saver especially on my blonde hairs that can be much harder to see.<br />My legs had red bumps after epilation, but the bumps went away in about 30 minutes. The red spots stayed for about an hour or two, so it's best to do this before bed. Another thing I like is that you can use this while it is charging (great option actually) just can't get it wet.<br /><br />My advice for after epilation to help soothe your legs and help keep away ingrown and infected hairs is take about a quarter sized amount of grape seed oil with 3-4 drops of tea tree oil and rub it all over your legs. There is a very very minor burning sensation afterwards, but it only lasts like 2 minutes. It makes the redness go away faster as well.<br /><br />FYI: my first epilation didn't leave my legs silky smooth, but that might be from some hairs being way way too short. It is best to epilate everyday for a few day so that the shorter hairs have time to grow out. Then the epilator can grab them. Also if you have hair that grows in multiple directions like I do, going in small circles seems to help.<br />Good luck!<br />Any questions don't hesitate to ask<br /><br />Another FYI: I forgot to mention this the first time I posted my review. I cannot stress enough how important exfoliating is. I recommend exfoliating before and after epilation. I do this by taking a shower/bath about an hour or two before I epilate. Then I wait till I'm about ready to go to bed, and then I usually run a quick bath just to exfoliate. This second bath is only in like a few inches of water and takes only a few minutes.

They do however help guide the head (the roller one anyway) so you can get smoother more controlled motions.<br /><br />The real gem here is the shaver though. My boyfriend has a Panasonic shaver (for men) with a very nice head...this is smaller but fairly comparable in function. It takes more passes over a hairy area than his does (we compared) but it also has smaller holes and less overall surface area. With its nice edge comb and all though I found this a FANTASTIC shaver...an worked on the legs just great! It's ridiculous I know, but I love the tweezer. It's in a little lipstick like tube and has a super bright LED for plucking. As much as I'd like to reserve it for eyebrows, the sucker is a great tweezer and just seems so darn useful I might keep it in my purse for general use (hey, LED flashlight!)<br />2) Bright light on the shaver/epilator. At first I thought this was ridiculous, but really wow it's nice! You see so many hairs that would get easily overlooked otherwise.<br />3) Power. It's quite powerful and has two speeds. More than enough power on the epilator for sure and the shaver seems pretty decent too.<br />4) Locking feature. There is a way to \\"lock\\" the shaver so you don't accidentally turn it on when storing it.<br />5) Can use while charging.<br />6) Plug in adapter is very tight...at least it won't fall out by accident.<br />7) Look. Nice if you paid for it and weren't sure if you'd like it or if you are concerned about it breaking or wearing out.<br />9) Shaver vs. epilator option. Even though I'm most likely to use this as a shaver, I like that the epilator is an option. As much as it pulls hair out my understanding is that epilation lasts a lot longer like waxing. It is indeed much smoother I can attest. Not sure I'll ever be able to use it on my legs though...I will try it again some time when I have longer hair on my legs and see if that helps or makes it worse. (See edit...longer hair is worse)<br />10) Smooth...I'll admit that in an area where you can stand to use it, the epilator does a fantastic job of leaving behind a very smooth surface...nearly as good as waxing. Just slower.<br />11) Easy to use. Other than the obnoxious instruction sheet (discussed in Cons) it was pretty intuitive. You can figure it out yourself very easily.<br />12) Very understandable charging indicators. Blinks brightly while charging, turns off when done (well actually turns solid and then turns off after a while, but unless you're watching it like a hawk...)<br />13) Seems very safe. I got confidence with it quickly and even though I didn't go out of my way to try cut myself, it seems very unlikely to injure you even when you're pressing hard or at angles (on the shaver). The same is true of the epilator really...it never seemed to present any danger other than yanking out hair.<br /><br />Cons:<br />1) Not waterproof or safe to use in the shower.<br />2) Ridiculous amount of instructions. For something that seems like it should be so simple, the instruction sheet is huge and confusing. There are 32 pictures to refer to and numerous steps. I skimmed most of it, but kept having to try look things up to make sure I was doing it right which was hard. It's not even a booklet. It's a fold out...the kind that never fold back as nice as they were before you unfolded it like an unruly old style map.<br />3) Can pop the head off while it's in use. The head comes off with a release on the side. Unfortunately if you hit this while it's running, the head comes off anyway and makes a partial connection. I don't know if you can damage the shaver this way but it seems like a real possibility.<br />4) Pain. Up to you...if you get used to it, I'm sure it's not so bad, but seriously, ow! It feels like an electric shock...that keeps shocking you until all the hair is gone.<br />5) Kinda messy...I admit seeing all the gross little hairs on the head and around where I was experimenting was unappealing. Shaving in the shower negates all that mess.<br />6) Not very fast. Honestly, a regular razor is faster even if you can't (or shouldn't) use it dry.<br />7) Tweezer batteries. As much as I like the tweezer I don't have anything else that uses coin cells that size. When it runs down it will be obnoxious to replace them.<br /><br />End verdict...I'll keep trying it and updating this review...I would probably never use the epilator on the pits but it's good on other areas you want super smooth. However, for an electric razor I'm very satisfied. Short of one that could be used in the shower like my boyfriend's the shaver portion is pretty much exactly what I was thinking of looking for at some point.   75. Disclaimer: I received this product free from BzzAgent to test and give my honest opinions.<br /><br />I've been epilating my legs for approximately 10 years now, and have used various cheap and expensive epilators. This one is my favorite! But before I get into the review, let me tell you The Secret of Epilating.<br /><br />What's the secret? Well, first, you need to choose a less sensitive area for your first epilating experiences. I suggest lower legs. After you get used to epilation there, you can move on to other areas if you wish. Now, here's the secret. The key to success...wax first!<br /><br />I know, you're thinking, \\"Wax! Whaaaat! I'm using an epilator so I don't have to wax or shave or do anything else!\\" Trust me. The amount of pain that an epilator will cause you is directly related to how many hairs it's yanking out. That goes for this epilator or any other epilator.<br /><br />So, get those lower legs waxed. You can go to a professional, which I recommend if you've never had waxing experience, or you can do it yourself with the home kits. You only need to do it this one time.<br /><br />Okay, so you've had your legs waxed. It hurt some, or a lot. You got through it. Now, enjoy those smooth legs for a week or two. After a week or two, you'll notice some short hairs starting to poke out and ruin that wonderful smooth leg experience. This is the time to epilate. Since there are only a few hairs getting yanked out, the pain will be bearable, and it won't take much time to do. After the initial epilation, you'll continue doing it every week or two in order to keep stubble at bay and keep the epilation relatively painless. Easy! If you get lazy and let the hair grow for weeks, you will notice that the pain gets worse. If, like me, you sometimes get super lazy in the winter and ignore your legs for months, there is always the option of starting over with the initial waxing cycle.<br /><br />Now you know the secret to epilation. So what's great about this epilator? Because, let's face it, this thing is expensive. (There is a similar, cheaper, model which doesn't include the electric razor attachment, which I will mention later.) Well, like I said, I have used various epilators over the years. This one seems to cause me the least amount of pain, but even more importantly, the fewest ingrown hairs. When epilating (with any epilator) there is always the chance that a hair, instead of being pulled out completely, will break off at the surface of the skin or just underneath. This, for me, can lead to ingrown hairs. This Satin Perfect Epilator, however it's different than others, (maybe the fact that the discs are ceramic instead of metal?) has not been causing that problem in the month and a half I've been using it. That aspect alone is well worth the price difference for me. If my house burned down or someone stole my epilator, I'd suck it up and pay to get another Satin Perfect.<br /><br />The cordless aspect is my other favorite thing about this epilator. It charges quickly and the charge lasts through several epilation cycles. You can use it anywhere (as long as it's dry; this is not for in-shower use) and you are not tied to a power outlet. However, if you need to epilate and the device is not charged, you can use it while it's plugged in and charging. Very convenient!<br /><br />The epilator head comes with two attachments you can add on. One is intended to massage/stretch the skin to make epilation easier; the other is intended to pull hairs up to make it easier for the epilator to catch them and pull them out. I tried them out and for me, they made the process less painful, but it took a little longer than normal. If you're new to epilation, I suggest trying them. If you're a veteran epilator, they are probably not necessary.<br /><br />In addition to the epilator head, this device comes with an electric razor head. The cheaper, non-deluxe version does not include this. I think it's pretty neat that you can use the device for both shaving and epilating. So this is not only a cordless epilator, it's also a cordless electric razor. Again, remember you are not supposed to be using this in the shower. The razor head worked well for me. I used it for shaving my upper legs and armpits--even though I've epilated for years, those areas are too sensitive for me to epilate. While the shave it gave was probably not as close as what I'd get with a disposable razor, my skin was less irritated. The shaver head also comes with a trimmer guard attachment.<br /><br />Overall, this is an expensive personal grooming device, but it is well worth it. A good epilator will last you for years. You'll save money on razors and shaving cream, and you won't be creating waste from disposable razors or blades. Your legs will be a lot smoother, and you'll spend less time on hair removal. As I said earlier, I did receive this product for free, but I would gladly pay to replace it if necessary.

Touch ups are necessary, but not as traumatic as a full epilation the first time. In fact, after the first time, it's really not bad at all. For the first time, go easy, work in segments so that you can see progress -- take your time. Another thing that is seldom mentioned is the need for exfoliation. You need to do this at least a couple of times a week in the shower so that you don't get ingrown hairs, which really are a pain. Simply scrub your legs with a loofah or brush to get the dead skin out of the way and apply lotion liberally. Should be good to go.

The ceramic heads are awesome. They're very safe. I read reviews of people who ripped up their skin with other epilators that have metal heads. Honestly, in the pictures of those epilators they look like some sort of strange torture devices. The ceramic heads on the Philips are very simple looking and not scary at all. They have never damaged my skin, and I don't think they even could. Twice, while epilating, my hand has slipped and my finger has jammed right into the spinning heads. Nothing happened. Somehow, this epilator is able to remove hairs from my underarm without touching the skin tag I have there. I don't know how it's possible, but it's true.<br />2. I love the fact that I can use this epilator while it's charging. I have two kids and a busy life (who doesn't?) and I need my epilator to be ready when I am. I get 2 full sessions in each time before re-charging anyway, but if the orange light comes on while I'm in the middle of a leg I just plug in and keep going. The cord is long enough to reach from the outlet by the sink to the toilet, which I sit on while doing my legs. It charges in about an hour, so I don't have to leave it sitting out all day.<br />3. The different heads and attachments are a nice addition, and I think they may be helpful to someone who is more sensitive to the pain. I quickly left them all behind and just use the regular one so I can get it over with as quickly as possible.<br />4. The head and attachments come apart and you can run them all under water to clean them. It takes me about 20 seconds to clean everything, then I set the pieces out to air-dry overnight. You really need it to be able to see where the hairs are, especially behind the knees and such.<br />6. The instructions are stupid and badly written.<br /><br />Those are the only bad things I can think of. Luckily, they do not detract from the overall usefulness of the epilator. I've been using this epilator for about 6 months now, and if it broke tomorrow I would not hesitate to buy the exact same one again.<br /><br />And now for my story on epilating in general . . .<br /><br />I can't shave.<br />I have eczema, skin tags, double follicles, and ingrown hairs.<br />I used to shave, and it was horribly painful. Not to mention the fact that I have very thick, dark hair that grows super fast, so even after enduring the pain of shaving, I would have stubble within 24 hours. I have the kind of hair that looks like it has 5 o'clock shadow immediately. I finally decided that shaving was no longer an option, so I looked for another solution.<br /><br />I tried epilating. I bought an Emjoi from Target (this was several years ago).<br />It hurt so bad I cried. I ended up just giving it away.<br />I spent the next couple of years trying to just be hairy. It's hard to do this. People do not react well to a woman with hairy armpits at the swimming pool. Especially when the hair is dark and wiry hair like mine.<br /><br />I decided to start getting waxed. Double ouch. Waxing was extremely painful, bad for my sensitive skin, very expensive, time-consuming, and still didn't work all that well. I expected to come home from the salon with baby-smooth skin that would stay hair-free for weeks. Nope. They never could quite get every hair, and I would have stubble in just a few days, even after repeatedly waxing for months. I found a lady in town who could do sugaring, which is MUCH better than waxing. It was far less painful, though still painful, and far better for my skin. Still very costly and time-consuming, and still no long-term results. I could wear a sleeveless shirt and shorts for about 5 days before I would have to cover myself up again. And then I would have to wait for 6-8 weeks before my next appointment. This was obviously not working.<br /><br />I began to feel desperate. Despite all of the drawbacks, I decided to just go back to shaving with an electric razor, but when I was looking them up on Amazon I came across the list of epilators. I knew it was possible that if I bought one I would use it once, cry my eyes out, and give it away just like I had with the Emjoi years ago, and that's a lot of money to throw away. I thought about it for a long time and finally figured I would just try to find a way to deal with the pain somehow. I spent many hours agonizing over every product and every review, and I couldn't decide which one to try.<br />I finally chose the Philips Satin Perfect simply based on the fact that it looked the classiest, ha!<br />I'm so glad I did.<br />I love it.<br />Epilating doesn't hurt me anymore, well, it's not completely free of pain, but it is absolutely tolerable. The first time I sat down to use it I was so nervous. When I tentatively put it to my leg and felt how little pain there was I actually laughed out loud.<br />I think all of those waxings and sugarings must have made me less sensitive.<br />It takes 20-30 minutes to do my legs and underarms, the results last several days, and I can sit down and do it again any time without having to wait for weeks. I can get hair-free in a half hour any time I want.<br />Seriously.
